     <div class="a-row">           <div id="revMH" class="a-column a-span11">                  <h3 class="a-spacing-small">Most Helpful Customer Reviews</h3> <div id="revMHRL" class="a-section">                            <div id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RIOWPF15RFFN0" class="a-section"><div class="a-row a-spacing-micro"><span class="a-size-small a-color-secondary">25 of 26 people found the following review helpful</span><div class="a-icon-row a-spacing-none"><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" title="4.0 out of 5 stars" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RIOWPF15RFFN0/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/189-8614298-9601032?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B008CXTW5G&nodeID=541966&store=pc"><i class="a-icon a-icon-star a-star-4"></i></a><span class="a-letter-space"></span><a class="a-link-normal a-text-normal a-color-base" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RIOWPF15RFFN0/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/189-8614298-9601032?ie=UTF8&ASIN=B008CXTW5G&nodeID=541966&store=pc"><span class="a-size-base a-text-bold">Decent mechanical keyboard but not great.</span></a></div><span class="a-color-secondary">         <span class="a-size-normal">     <span class="a-color-secondary">       By     </span>     <a href="/gp/pdp/profile/AHHOLC03U9BDS/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/189-8614298-9601032" class="noTextDecoration">Dave</a>   </span> <span class="a-color-secondary"> on August 27, 2012</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-RIOWPF15RFFN0" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   <span class="MHRHead">I purchased this keyboard to replace my Logitech G15.  Searching around I couldn't find any place nearby that had mechanical keyboards to test the feel of the different switches so I was left to blindly choose which one I thought would work the best for me.  I went with the black instead of the reds to try to alleviate any accidental key presses.  The blacks are very stiff.  About as stiff as a normal membrane keyboard - which isn't really a bad thing.  My first impressions of the keyboard were very positive.  It looked nice, had a nice weight to it, the large rubber feet with multiple adjustments were great, you could customize the setup between the DPad and the num pad, overall it was an impressive keyboard.<br><br>Being able to adjust the location of the DPad for macro keys is a great idea.  However, this removes the ability to use the function keys at the top of the keyboard.  Most games don't use these, but things like Alt+F4 has it's use in certain situations.  Being up so high I didn't find these to be in a great location.  I stuck to using the macro keys to the left of the keyboard.<br><br>One thing I noticed quickly was the sharpness of the corners on the keys.  When gaming I press the space bar with the side of my thumb.  My old G15 had an oversized space bar so I simply just pressed down on the middle of the key.  The Mech5 has a normal sized space bar.  This resulted in me pressing down on the corner of the key.  After a short while of gaming my thumb became sore and irritated.  It was a simple adjustment to move my thumb a bit higher on the keyboard, but it was an unnatural adjustment.<br><br>Another thing I noticed was the markings on the keys were not consistent.  The left shift in particular was very light - as if it had been used for a long time.</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot;  How I place my finger on the shift key I don&#39;t press down on the lettering so it was definitely not from use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I knew going into it that the Mech5 didn&#39;t have any backlighting and I was okay with that.  Until I actually used it in dim lighting.  I can type upwards of 80 words a minute and have no problems finding even the rarest of symbols, but it was natural just to glance down at the keyboard from time to time for whatever reason.  The lack of backlighting isn&#39;t a huge deal but they included a bit of it on the macro keys with a really nice red - why not just use this throughout the rest of the keyboard?  This also would have alleviated my above complaint about the cheap marking on the key caps themselves if they chose to have backlit keys.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After a few weeks of use I was still happy with the keyboard, but wasn&#39;t blown away like I was hoping to be.  The sound and feel of the mechanical keys were great.  Gaming on it felt more natural than a traditional keyboard as keystrokes could be performed faster.  But again, with the Cherry MX Black switches being so stiff it didn&#39;t feel like a vast improvement.  I ended up purchasing a Corsair K90 in order to see how big of a difference there was between the blacks and the Cherry MX reds.  I have to say, I easily prefer the reds.  The blacks are nice, but don&#39;t have too different of a feel of a traditional keyboard except that they are linear and travel downwards very smoothly instead of the uneven resistance of typical rubber membranes.  The reds are very sensitive, but not to the point where you can&#39;t touch the other keys without them being activated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I ended up returning the Azio Mech5 and keeping the Corsair K90.  The K90 for the same price had a few added features like multimedia keys and a mute button.  The large dial of the Azio was nice, but with the lack of a mute button it took several full rotations to quiet the noise.  The K90 is an absolutely beautiful keyboard with the aluminum and tons of backlighting.  The Azio is a striking keyboard as well with its massive frame and aggressive styling.  The two are very different from every aspect and it ultimately comes down to a matter of taste.  I was happy with the Azio Mech5 but for the same price the Corsair K90 is a slightly better product.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would recommend the Azio Mech5 to anyone if they prefer black switches over reds.  If the reds are too sensitive for you and you love blacks, the Azio is a great choice.  Just know that it has a few shortcomings.  If it would have had backlighting and better keycaps and a mute button I probably would have stuck with it.  Many of the mechanical keyboards don&#39;t have any multimedia keys or volume dials and many don&#39;t have macro functionality so the Azio definitely has it&#39;s place.  Unfortunately, it just wasn&#39;t for me.  I really liked the keyboard, but I didn&#39;t $100 like it.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal" It really does remind me of the older, more indestructible keyboards.<br><br>Overall, I would rate this product a 4.5/5<br><br>Some of the really nice perks of this keyboard:<br>- The keys are very strong<br>- The volume knob appears to be more accurate than the Mech4 (it takes less turning to adjust the volume)<br>- You can detach the num pad and macro pad and use them individually<br>- There is a quick way to disable the windows keys<br>- It is nice and heavy, don't have to worry about it moving around<br>- You can customize every key on the keyboard using the software that comes with it<br>- The "\" and "|" key is above the enter key (and not beside the backspace key like the Mech4)<br>- The "Enter" key is in a normal position<br><br>Some of the shortcomings of this keyboard:<br>- Clackity-Clackity-Clack (It is very noisy)<br>- Nothing else that I can think of!<br><br>I would highly recommend this keyboard for both gamers and power users alike.<br><br>It is a GREAT keyboard! Goetowski</a>   </span> <span class="a-declarative" data-action="cr-popup" data-cr-popup="{&quot;width&quot;:340,&quot;title&quot;:&quot;AmazonHelp&quot;,&quot;height&quot;:340}" style="display:inline;"></span><span class="a-color-secondary"> on January 6, 2013</span></span></div><div id="revData-dpReviewsMostHelpfulAUI-R2GYX2TMJ3TLRB" class="a-row a-spacing-small"><span class="a-size-mini a-color-state a-text-bold">     Verified Purchase   </span>      <div class="a-section">   <span class="MHRHead">This particular keyboard functions as advertised in the box description, and I can appreciate how the manufacturer points out a few obscure, slightly unintuitive dos and don'ts in the manual, but more on that later.<br><br>I'll start with the (relatively) bad, and then move on to the good.<br><br>-BAD<br><br>Firstly, the modular design necessitates that the 'main' keyboard component is rather cramped, and given the placement of the 'A/B' function keys on the left side, it's easy to accidentally hit a key adjacent to the one you meant to hit as your hands adjust to being closer together than they would be with a more spacious, non-modular keyboard. This problem works itself out in time, though, so it's not too big a deal if typing isn't your livelihood.<br><br>Next is the absence of any backlighting for the keys, which is something I kinda got used to with my previous keyboard (Saitek Cyborg, first revision). I can understand the impracticality of adding backlighting to mechanical keys, but it would have been nice if Azio had added a lamp or something to be used on the top 'rail' that holds the 'D-function' pad.<br><br>Lastly, I'm a little disappointed in the lack of any microphone and/or headphone jacks housed right next to the two USB ports by the volume knob (one of which is already going to be occupied by the D-function pad, should you choose to use it).<br><br>-Good<br><br>Two words: Limitless customisability. At least as far as tagging macros to keys is concerned. This makes up for the lack of any dedicated media player or web browser command keys, since you can use the profile software to set those functions to either the A/B function keys, the D-function pad, or any of the standard keys.</span><span class="a-declarative" data-action="columnbalancing-showfullreview" data-columnbalancing-showfullreview="{&quot;rest&quot;:&quot; It&#39;s great for gaming, whether it be an old DOSBox game (DOSBox has an internal keymapper that can be used to tag joystick macros to keys, but it&#39;s a little daunting for users not familiar with editing .ini files and the like), or even MMO&#39;s (you can type in your own TeamChat lines for instant entry with the press of a button). It&#39;s also good for productivity programs like word processors (Tired of pressing ALT+#### just to make an umlaut? Tag it to a macro!).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Next let&#39;s talk about construction. Classic, sturdy-feeling, matte-finished plastic. No cheap, hollow plastics with gaudy gloss finishes here. The moment you press down on the first key you type with, you know you&#39;re using something well-built that&#39;s going to last. Add cloth-covered USB cords with gold-plated connectors, and you&#39;ve got a winner.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I mentioned at the beginning how the manual points out some stuff that not many people think about. One of these is how you should only connect &#39;low-powered&#39; USB devices, such as mice, gamepads, etc., to the onboard USB ports. This will save you a call to tech support when you can&#39;t get your webcam or external hard disk to work. You can&#39;t use the ports to charge a phone or use a USB headset with super-mega-high-fidelity, 24-channel uber-surround sound.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line: The money you spend on this is spent more on function than form. It&#39;s not got all the latest stuff like built-in LCD screen or whatever, but it&#39;s built to last, so you won&#39;t be spending a lot to replace it anytime soon. Provided, of course, that &#39;anytime soon&#39; doesn&#39;t herald the introduction of a new HID standard.&quot;}"><a class="a-link-normal" I used to never use Macro keys because of all the awkward locations that keyboard manufacturers put them. I mean, by the time I reach over and hit the right macro key, I could have executed the command string manually, kind of defeats the purpose. With the D-Pad though, I'm basically reassigning all my hard to reach command keys onto the D-Pad as well as certain command chains. For example, on SC2, I've reassigned the number keys 8, 9, 0 unto D4, D5, and D6 and I'm assigning special tactic troops onto those keys for more strategic plays. The location of these D keys makes it very easy for me to access and use... It's definitely improved my game but it's kind of spoiled me and I feel naked playing on any other keyboard now LOL.<br><br>Anyhow - the rest of the keyboard is also of good quality build and the Cherry black mechanical switch is perfect for gaming. The detachable numpad makes the keyboard excessively big -thank god it's detachable... I leave it off and never use it. Overall - I strongly recommend this keyboard for gaming! </div>  </div>        <a class="a-link-normal comment-link" title="0"
